Colour name: Green, shortcode <code>[colour-brand-green]</code><br />
Colour name: Pale Blue Background, shortcode  <code>[colour-brand-pale-blue-background]</code><br /><br />

This name version of the shortcode is the main one that should be used. However, brand colour shortcodes are also created in the ranked order below, eg. <code>[colour-brand-1]</code>. Therefore the primary brand colour should be in position 1, the secondary brand colour in position 2, and so on.<br /><br />

CSS classes for the brand colours can be created by turning the Colour Classes and/or Background Colour Classes on. This will create colour classes that can be applied to elements as desired (the classes themselves will appear after Colour Schemes in the CSS file). Classes take the format <code>.colour-{name}</code>] or <code>.background-colour-{name}] </code> (where {name} is the name of the colour in lower case with hyphens instead of spaces).<br /><br />

Examples of this in HTML for the colour name "Red":<br /><br />

<code>&lt;h3 class="colour-red"&gt;<br />
&lt;div class="background-colour-red"&gt;</code><br /><br />

Heading colours for a section can also be overwritten by using a developer class. To set this up, turn on Heading Colours. This will create CSS for <code>.heading-{name}</code> (to affect only h1 and h2 headings within the section) and <code>.headings-{name}</code> (to affect all headings within the section).<br /><br />
